```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching

4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Incident Root-Cause: Grafana Dashboard Migration Field Config Loss

## Your Task

A Grafana dashboard migration (v38) silently drops table panel field override configuration during import. Dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` lose column widths and text alignment. Trace this bug to its root cause in the Grafana codebase. Find: 1. The Go source files under `pkg/services/dashboardimport/` or `pkg/services/dashboards/` that implement the v38 schema migration. 2. The specific function that handles `fieldConfig` merging and the conditional logic that fails for missing `defaults.custom`. 3. The schema version constant file that registers v38. Report the repo, file path, function name, and the flawed conditional expression for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
```

77-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the root cause of the Grafana dashboard migration v38 bug. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I've identified the **critical bug in the v38 schema migration** that silently drops table panel field override configuration:

### **Root Cause Location**
- **File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`
- **Function:** `processPanelsV38()` 
- **Flawed Code (Lines 116-117):**
```go
if defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {
    if custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {
```

### **The Problem**
The nested conditional checks only process if `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` exists, but **fails to create it when missing**. For dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`:

1. Line 116 passes (defaults exists)
2. Line 117 fails (custom doesn't exist)
3. The entire processing block (lines 118-126) is skipped
4. During cleanup, empty `fieldConfig.defaults` is removed because no marker preserved it
5. Field overrides referencing custom properties (minWidth, align, etc.) become orphaned
6. Configuration is silently lost

### **Key Files Identified**
1. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`** - Contains the flawed migration logic
2. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go`** - Registers v38 migration (line 74)
3. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`** - Related cleanup/tracking logic

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details including the call chain and detailed technical explanation of the bug mechanism.

ok` - This PASSES (defaults exists)\\n   - Line 117 checks: `if custom, ok := defaults[\\\"custom\\\"]...; ok` - This FAILS (custom doesn't exist)\\n   - Lines 118-126 are skipped entirely\\n   - Line 131 calls `migrateOverrides()`, which only migrates \\\"custom.displayMode\\\" references\\n\\n4. **Cleanup Phase:**\\n   - The cleanup function evaluates whether `fieldConfig.defaults` should be preserved\\n   - Since NO marker was set (because custom didn't originally exist), the cleanup removes empty `fieldConfig.defaults`\\n   - Field overrides that reference custom properties (minWidth, align, etc.) now point to a non-existent structure\\n   - Result: Configuration loss\\n\\n## The Flawed Conditional Expression\\n\\n**File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`  \\n**Function:** `processPanelsV38()`  \\n**Lines:** 116-117\\n\\n```go\\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\\\"defaults\\\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\\n    if custom, ok := defaults[\\\"custom\\\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\\n```\\n\\nThe issue is that these nested conditionals:\\n1. Only process if BOTH defaults AND custom exist as maps\\n2. Do NOT create/ensure custom exists when it's needed\\n3. Leave overrides orphaned when custom doesn't exist\\n\\n## Required Fix\\n\\nThe code should ensure `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` exists before processing overrides, even if it wasn't in the original input:\\n\\n```go\\n// Ensure defaults.custom exists for override processing\\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\\\"defaults\\\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\\n    // Ensure custom object exists\\n    if _, hasCustom := defaults[\\\"custom\\\"]; !hasCustom {\\n        defaults[\\\"custom\\\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\\n    }\\n    // Now safely process custom\\n    if custom, ok := defaults[\\\"custom\\\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\\n        // ... migration logic ...\\n    }\\n}\\n```\\n\\nAlternatively, the tracking system should mark panels as having custom if they have any overrides referencing custom properties, not just if they had custom in the input.\"\n}\n",
